</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Asia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="/ʒ/: 's' in 'pleasure'">ʒ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>, <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Asia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/En-us-Asia.ogg" title="En-us-Asia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>) is <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>'s largest and most populous <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a>, located primarily in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemisphere_of_the_Earth" title="Hemisphere of the Earth">Hemispheres</a>. It shares the continental landmass of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> with the continent of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and the continental landmass of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">Afro-Eurasia</a> with both Europe and Africa. Asia covers an area of 44,579,000 square kilometres (17,212,000 sq mi), about 30% of Earth's total land area and 8.7% of the Earth's total surface area. The continent, which has long been home to the majority of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_population" title="Human population">human population</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> was the site of many of the <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">first civilizations</a>. Asia is notable for not only its overall large size and population, but also dense and large settlements as well as vast barely populated regions within the continent of 4.5 billion people, or roughly 60% of the world's population.</p>
<p>In general terms, Asia is bounded on the east by the Pacific Ocean, on the south by the Indian Ocean and on the north by the Arctic Ocean. The western boundary with Europe is a historical and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_construct" title="Cultural construct">cultural construct</a>, as there is no clear physical and geographical separation between them. The most commonly accepted boundaries place Asia to the east of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>, and south of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Seas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>China and India alternated in being the <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_by_past_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of regions by past GDP (PPP)">largest economies in the world</a> from 1 to 1800 CE. China was a major economic power and attracted many to the east,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> and for many the legendary wealth and prosperity of the ancient culture of India personified Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> attracting European commerce, exploration and colonialism. The accidental discovery of America by Columbus in search for India demonstrates this deep fascination. The <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> became the main East-West trading route in the Asian hinterlands while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Straits_of_Malacca" title="Straits of Malacca">Straits of Malacca</a> stood as a major sea route. Asia has exhibited economic dynamism (particularly East Asia) as well as robust population growth during the 20th century, but overall population growth has since fallen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Asia was the birthplace of most of the world's mainstream religions including Christianity, Islam, Judaism, Hinduism, Buddhism, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, Taoism (or Daoism), <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoroastranism" title="Zoroastranism">Zoroastranism</a>, as well as many other religions.</p>
<p>Given its size and diversity, the concept of Asia—a <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">name</a> dating back to <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>—may actually have more to do with <a href="/wiki/Human_geography" title="Human geography">human geography</a> than <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">physical geography</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McG-H_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-McG-H-11">[11]</a></sup> Asia varies greatly across and within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regions_of_Asia" title="Regions of Asia">its regions</a> with regard to ethnic groups, cultures, environments, economics, historical ties and government systems. It also has a mix of many different climates ranging from the equatorial south via the hot desert in the Middle East, temperate areas in the east and the continental centre to vast subarctic and polar areas in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition_and_boundaries">Definition and boundaries</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For more details on Asian borders, see <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Asia#Boundary" title="Geography of Asia">Geography of Asia § Boundary</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boundaries_between_continents" title="Boundaries between continents">Boundaries between continents</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries#Asia_and_Europe" title="List of transcontinental countries">List of transcontinental countries § Asia and Europe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a>.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia-Africa_boundary">Asia-Africa boundary</span></h3>
<p>The boundary between Asia and Africa is the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Suez" title="Gulf of Suez">Gulf of Suez</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>. This makes <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">transcontinental country</a>, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinai_peninsula" title="Sinai peninsula">Sinai peninsula</a> in Asia and the remainder of the country in Africa.</p>
<h3><span id="Asia–Europe_boundary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia.E2.80.93Europe_boundary">Asia–Europe boundary</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Ferreria_statue.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1936" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Palazzo_Ferreria_statue.jpeg/220px-Palazzo_Ferreria_statue.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Palazzo_Ferreria_statue.jpeg/330px-Palazzo_Ferreria_statue.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Palazzo_Ferreria_statue.jpeg/440px-Palazzo_Ferreria_statue.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Ferreria_statue.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue representing Asia at <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Ferreria" title="Palazzo Ferreria">Palazzo Ferreria</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The border between Asia and Europe was historically defined by European academics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatGeo_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-NatGeo-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Don_River_(Russia)" title="Don River (Russia)">Don River</a> became unsatisfactory to northern Europeans when <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>, king of the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a>, defeating rival claims of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> to the eastern lands, and armed resistance by the tribes of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, synthesized a new <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> extending to the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> and beyond, founded in 1721. The major geographical theorist of the empire was actually a former Swedish prisoner-of-war, taken at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Poltava" title="Battle of Poltava">Battle of Poltava</a> in 1709 and assigned to <a href="/wiki/Tobolsk" title="Tobolsk">Tobolsk</a>, where he associated with Peter's Siberian official, <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Tatishchev" title="Vasily Tatishchev">Vasily Tatishchev</a>, and was allowed freedom to conduct geographical and anthropological studies in preparation for a future book.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In Sweden, five years after Peter's death, in 1730 <a href="/wiki/Philip_Johan_von_Strahlenberg" title="Philip Johan von Strahlenberg">Philip Johan von Strahlenberg</a> published a new atlas proposing the Urals as the border of Asia. The Russians were enthusiastic about the concept, which allowed them to keep their European identity in geography. Tatishchev announced that he had proposed the idea to von Strahlenberg. The latter had suggested the <a href="/wiki/Emba_River" title="Emba River">Emba River</a> as the lower boundary. Over the next century various proposals were made until the <a href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a> prevailed in the mid-19th century. The border had been moved perforce from the Black Sea to the Caspian Sea into which the Ural River projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The border between the Black Sea and the Caspian is usually placed along the crest of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a>, although it is sometimes placed further north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatGeo_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-NatGeo-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Asia–Oceania_boundary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia.E2.80.93Oceania_boundary">Asia–Oceania boundary</span></h3>
<p>The border between Asia and the region of <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> is usually placed somewhere in the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">Malay Archipelago</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a> in Indonesia are often considered to lie on the border of southeast Asia, with <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, to the east of the islands, being wholly part of Oceania. The terms Southeast Asia and Oceania, devised in the 19th century, have had several vastly different geographic meanings since their inception. The chief factor in determining which islands of the Malay Archipelago are Asian has been the location of the colonial possessions of the various empires there (not all European). Lewis and Wigen assert, "The narrowing of 'Southeast Asia' to its present boundaries was thus a gradual process."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Myth_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Myth-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ongoing_definition">Ongoing definition</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afro-Eurasia_(orthographic_projection).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="550" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/220px-Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/330px-Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/440px-Afro-Eurasia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afro-Eurasia_(orthographic_projection).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">Afro-Eurasia</a> shown in green</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Geographical Asia is a cultural artifact of European conceptions of the world, beginning with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greeks" title="Ancient Greeks">Ancient Greeks</a>, being imposed onto other cultures, an imprecise concept causing endemic contention about what it means. Asia is larger and more culturally diverse than Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> It does not exactly correspond to the cultural borders of its various types of constituents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the time of <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> a minority of geographers have rejected the three-continent system (Europe, Africa, Asia) on the grounds that there is no or is no substantial physical separation between them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McG-H_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-McG-H-11">[11]</a></sup> For example, Sir <a href="/wiki/Barry_Cunliffe" title="Barry Cunliffe">Barry Cunliffe</a>, the emeritus professor of European archeology at Oxford, argues that Europe has been geographically and culturally merely "the western excrescence of the continent of Asia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Geographically, Asia is the major eastern constituent of the continent of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> with Europe being a northwestern <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> of the landmass. Asia, Europe and Africa make up a single continuous landmass - <a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">Afro-Eurasia</a> (except for the Suez Canal) and share a common <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a>. Almost all of Europe and the better part of Asia sit atop the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a>, adjoined on the south by the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Plate" title="Arabian Plate">Arabian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Plate" title="Indian Plate">Indian Plate</a> and with the easternmost part of Siberia (east of the <a href="/wiki/Chersky_Range" title="Chersky Range">Chersky Range</a>) on the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plate</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gulf5..JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gulf5..JPG/300px-Gulf5..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gulf5..JPG/450px-Gulf5..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gulf5..JPG/600px-Gulf5..JPG 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gulf5..JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ptolemy's Asia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The English name "Asia" was originally a concept of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_civilization" title="Greek civilization">Greek civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reid_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-reid-18">[18]</a></sup> The place name "Asia" in various forms in a large number of modern languages is of unknown ultimate provenience. Its etymology and language of origin are uncertain. It appears to be one of the most ancient of recorded names. A number of theories have been published. English Asia can be traced through the formation of English literature to Latin literature, where it has the same form, Asia. Whether all uses and all forms of the name derive also from the Latin of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> is much less certain. One of the first classical writers to use Asia as a name of the whole continent was <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">metonymical</a> change in meaning is common and can be observed in some other geographical names, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skandinavia" title="Skandinavia">Skandinavia</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Scania" title="Scania">Scania</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bronze_Age">Bronze Age</span></h3>
<p>Before Greek poetry, the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> area was in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_Dark_Age" title="Greek Dark Age">Greek Dark Age</a>, at the beginning of which syllabic writing was lost and alphabetic writing had not begun. Prior to then in the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> the records of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_Empire" title="Assyrian Empire">Assyrian Empire</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hittite_Empire" title="Hittite Empire">Hittite Empire</a> and the various <a href="/wiki/Mycenaean_Greece" title="Mycenaean Greece">Mycenaean</a> states of Greece mention a region undoubtedly Asia, certainly in Anatolia, including if not identical to Lydia. These records are administrative and do not include poetry.</p>
<p>The Mycenaean states were destroyed about 1200 BCE by unknown agents although one school of thought assigns the <a href="/wiki/Dorian_invasion" title="Dorian invasion">Dorian invasion</a> to this time. The burning of the palaces baked clay diurnal administrative records written in a Greek syllabic script called <a href="/wiki/Linear_B" title="Linear B">Linear B</a>, deciphered by a number of interested parties, most notably by a young World War II cryptographer, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ventris" title="Michael Ventris">Michael Ventris</a>, subsequently assisted by the scholar, <a href="/wiki/John_Chadwick" title="John Chadwick">John Chadwick</a>. A major cache discovered by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Blegen" title="Carl Blegen">Carl Blegen</a> at the site of ancient <a href="/wiki/Pylos" title="Pylos">Pylos</a> included hundreds of male and female names formed by different methods.</p>
<p>Some of these are of women held in servitude (as study of the society implied by the content reveals). They were used in trades, such as cloth-making, and usually came with children. The epithet, lawiaiai, "captives," associated with some of them identifies their origin. Some are ethnic names. One in particular, aswiai, identifies "women of Asia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Perhaps they were captured in Asia, but some others, Milatiai, appear to have been of <a href="/wiki/Miletus" title="Miletus">Miletus</a>, a Greek colony, which would not have been raided for slaves by Greeks. Chadwick suggests that the names record the locations where these foreign women were purchased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The name is also in the singular, Aswia, which refers both to the name of a country and to a female of it. There is a masculine form, aswios. This Aswia appears to have been a remnant of a region known to the Hittites as Assuwa, centered on Lydia, or "Roman Asia." This name, <i>Assuwa</i>, has been suggested as the origin for the name of the continent "Asia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assuwa_league" title="Assuwa league">Assuwa league</a> was a confederation of states in western Anatolia, defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittites</a> under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tudhaliya_I" title="Tudhaliya I">Tudhaliya I</a> around 1400 BCE.</p>
<p>Alternatively, the <a href="/wiki/Etymology" title="Etymology">etymology</a> of the term may be from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akkadian_language" title="Akkadian language">Akkadian</a> word <i>(w)aṣû(m)</i>, which means 'to go outside' or 'to ascend', referring to the direction of the sun at sunrise in the Middle East and also likely connected with the Phoenician word <i>asa</i> meaning east. This may be contrasted to a similar etymology proposed for <i>Europe</i>, as being from Akkadian <i>erēbu(m)</i> 'to enter' or 'set' (of the sun).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/T.R._Reid" title="T.R. Reid">T.R. Reid</a> supports this alternative etymology, noting that the ancient Greek name must have derived from <i>asu</i>, meaning 'east' in <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrian</a> (<i>ereb</i> for <i>Europe</i> meaning 'west').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reid_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-reid-18">[18]</a></sup> The ideas of <i>Occidental</i> (form <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>Occidens</i> 'setting') and <i>Oriental</i> (from Latin <i>Oriens</i> for 'rising') are also European invention, synonymous with <i>Western</i> and <i>Eastern</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reid_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-reid-18">[18]</a></sup> Reid further emphasizes that it explains the Western point of view of placing all the peoples and cultures of Asia into a single classification, almost as if there were a need for setting the distinction between Western and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">Eastern civilizations</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasian</a> continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reid_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-reid-18">[18]</a></sup> Ogura Kazuo and Tenshin Okakura are two outspoken Japanese figures on the subject.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reid_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-reid-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_antiquity">Classical antiquity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_-_Asia_(125_AD).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1817" data-file-width="2186" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg/220px-Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg/330px-Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg/440px-Roman_Empire_-_Asia_%28125_AD%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_-_Asia_(125_AD).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The province of <a href="/wiki/Asia_(Roman_province)" title="Asia (Roman province)">Asia</a> highlighted (in red) within the Roman Empire.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Latin Asia and Greek Ἀσία appear to be the same word. Roman authors translated Ἀσία as Asia. The Romans named a province <a href="/wiki/Asia_(Roman_province)" title="Asia (Roman province)">Asia</a>, which roughly corresponds with modern-day central-western Turkey. There was an Asia Minor and an Asia Major located in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. As the earliest evidence of the name is Greek, it is likely circumstantially that Asia came from Ἀσία, but ancient transitions, due to the lack of literary contexts, are difficult to catch in the act. The most likely vehicles were the ancient geographers and historians, such as <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a>, who were all Greek. <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> certainly evidences early and rich uses of the name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first continental use of Asia is attributed to Herodotus (about 440 BCE), not because he innovated it, but because his <i>Histories</i> are the earliest surviving prose to describe it in any detail. He defines it carefully,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> mentioning the previous geographers whom he had read, but whose works are now missing. By it he means <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Persian Empire</a>, in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>. Herodotus comments that he is puzzled as to why three women's names were "given to a tract which is in reality one" (<a href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">Europa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia_(mythology)" title="Asia (mythology)">Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Libya_(mythology)" title="Libya (mythology)">Libya</a>, referring to Africa), stating that most Greeks assumed that Asia was named after the wife of <a href="/wiki/Prometheus" title="Prometheus">Prometheus</a> (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Hesione" title="Hesione">Hesione</a>), but that the <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydians</a> say it was named after Asies, son of Cotys, who passed the name on to a tribe at <a href="/wiki/Sardis" title="Sardis">Sardis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek mythology</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Asia_(mythology)" title="Asia (mythology)">Asia</a>" (<i>Ἀσία</i>) or "Asie" (<i>Ἀσίη</i>) was the name of a "<a href="/wiki/Nymph" title="Nymph">Nymph</a> or <a href="/wiki/Titan_(mythology)" title="Titan (mythology)">Titan</a> goddess of Lydia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In ancient Greek religion, places were under the care of female divinities, parallel to guardian angels. The poets detailed their doings and generations in allegoric language salted with entertaining stories, which subsequently playwrights transformed into classical Greek drama and became "Greek mythology." For example, <a href="/wiki/Hesiod" title="Hesiod">Hesiod</a> mentions the daughters of <a href="/wiki/Tethys_(mythology)" title="Tethys (mythology)">Tethys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceanus" title="Oceanus">Ocean</a>, among whom are a "holy company", "who with the Lord <a href="/wiki/Apollo" title="Apollo">Apollo</a> and the Rivers have youths in their keeping."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Many of these are geographic: Doris, Rhodea, Europa, Asia. Hesiod explains:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"For there are three-thousand neat-ankled daughters of Ocean who are dispersed far and wide, and in every place alike serve the earth and the deep waters."</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Iliad" title="Iliad">Iliad</a> (attributed by the ancient Greeks to <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a>) mentions two Phrygians (the tribe that replaced the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luvians" title="Luvians">Luvians</a> in Lydia) in the <a href="/wiki/Trojan_War" title="Trojan War">Trojan War</a> named <a href="/wiki/Asius_(mythology)" title="Asius (mythology)">Asios</a> (an adjective meaning "Asian");<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and also a marsh or lowland containing a marsh in Lydia as ασιος.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Asia" title="History of Asia">History of Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_dominions1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="938" data-file-width="1280" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mongol_dominions1.jpg/250px-Mongol_dominions1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mongol_dominions1.jpg/375px-Mongol_dominions1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Mongol_dominions1.jpg/500px-Mongol_dominions1.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_dominions1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>, ca. 1300. The gray area is the later <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid Empire</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asien_Bd1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1974" data-file-width="2500" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Asien_Bd1.jpg/250px-Asien_Bd1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Asien_Bd1.jpg/375px-Asien_Bd1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Asien_Bd1.jpg/500px-Asien_Bd1.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asien_Bd1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1890 map of Asia</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_Map_of_the_Countries_between_Constantinople_and_Calcutta-_Including_Turkey_in_Asia,_Persia,_Afghanistan_and_Turkestan_WDL11753.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1391" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/A_Map_of_the_Countries_between_Constantinople_and_Calcutta-_Including_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Persia%2C_Afghanistan_and_Turkestan_WDL11753.png/220px-A_Map_of_the_Countries_between_Constantinople_and_Calcutta-_Including_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Persia%2C_Afghanistan_and_Turkestan_WDL11753.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/A_Map_of_the_Countries_between_Constantinople_and_Calcutta-_Including_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Persia%2C_Afghanistan_and_Turkestan_WDL11753.png/330px-A_Map_of_the_Countries_between_Constantinople_and_Calcutta-_Including_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Persia%2C_Afghanistan_and_Turkestan_WDL11753.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/A_Map_of_the_Countries_between_Constantinople_and_Calcutta-_Including_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Persia%2C_Afghanistan_and_Turkestan_WDL11753.png/440px-A_Map_of_the_Countries_between_Constantinople_and_Calcutta-_Including_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Persia%2C_Afghanistan_and_Turkestan_WDL11753.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_Map_of_the_Countries_between_Constantinople_and_Calcutta-_Including_Turkey_in_Asia,_Persia,_Afghanistan_and_Turkestan_WDL11753.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of western, southern, and central Asia in 1885<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The history of Asia can be seen as the distinct histories of several peripheral coastal regions: East Asia, South Asia, Southeast Asia and the Middle East, linked by the interior mass of the Central Asian <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a>.</p>
<p>The coastal periphery was home to some of the world's earliest known civilizations, each of them developing around fertile river valleys. The civilizations in <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_Valley" title="Indus Valley">Indus Valley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> shared many similarities. These civilizations may well have exchanged technologies and ideas such as <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a> and the wheel. Other innovations, such as writing, seem to have been developed individually in each area. Cities, states and empires developed in these lowlands.</p>
<p>The central steppe region had long been inhabited by horse-mounted nomads who could reach all areas of Asia from the <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a>. The earliest postulated expansion out of the steppe is that of the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">Indo-Europeans</a>, who spread their languages into the Middle East, South Asia, and the borders of China, where the <a href="/wiki/Tocharians" title="Tocharians">Tocharians</a> resided. The northernmost part of Asia, including much of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, was largely inaccessible to the steppe nomads, owing to the dense forests, climate and <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a>. These areas remained very sparsely populated.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silkroutes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="660" data-file-width="750" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Silkroutes.jpg/250px-Silkroutes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Silkroutes.jpg/375px-Silkroutes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Silkroutes.jpg/500px-Silkroutes.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silkroutes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> connected many civilizations across Asia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The center and the peripheries were mostly kept separated by mountains and deserts. The <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Himalaya" title="Himalaya">Himalaya</a> mountains and the <a href="/wiki/Karakum_Desert" title="Karakum Desert">Karakum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi</a> deserts formed barriers that the steppe horsemen could cross only with difficulty. While the urban city dwellers were more advanced technologically and socially, in many cases they could do little in a military aspect to defend against the mounted hordes of the steppe. However, the lowlands did not have enough open grasslands to support a large horsebound force; for this and other reasons, the <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomads</a> who conquered states in China, India, and the Middle East often found themselves adapting to the local, more affluent societies.</p>
<p>The Islamic <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliphate</a> took over the Middle East and Central Asia during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_conquests" title="Muslim conquests">Muslim conquests</a> of the 7th century. The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> conquered a large part of Asia in the 13th century, an area extending from China to Europe. Before the Mongol invasion, <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> reportedly had approximately 120 million citizens; the 1300 census which followed the invasion reported roughly 60 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>, one of the most devastating <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemics</a> in human history, is thought to have originated in the arid plains of central Asia, where it then travelled along the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> began to expand into Asia from the 17th century, and would eventually take control of all of Siberia and most of Central Asia by the end of the 19th century. The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> controlled Anatolia, most of the Middle East, North Africa and the Balkans from the mid 16th century onwards. In the 17th century, the <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchu</a> conquered China and established the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a>. The Islamic <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a> and the Hindu <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Empire" title="Maratha Empire">Maratha Empire</a> controlled much of India in the 16th and 18th centuries respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Asia" title="Geography of Asia">Geography of Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Asia" title="Climate of Asia">Climate of Asia</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Biota_of_Asia" title="Category:Biota of Asia">Category:Biota of Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Himalayas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1998" data-file-width="3032" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Himalayas.jpg/220px-Himalayas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Himalayas.jpg/330px-Himalayas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Himalayas.jpg/440px-Himalayas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Himalayas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayan</a> range is home to some of the planet's highest peaks.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Asia is the largest <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a> on Earth. It covers 8.8% of the Earth's total surface area (or 30% of its land area), and has the largest coastline, at 62,800 kilometres (39,022 mi). Asia is generally defined as comprising the eastern four-fifths of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>. It is located to the east of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>, and south of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> (or the <a href="/wiki/Kuma%E2%80%93Manych_Depression" title="Kuma–Manych Depression">Kuma–Manych Depression</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Seas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-36">[36]</a></sup> It is bounded on the east by the Pacific Ocean, on the south by the Indian Ocean and on the north by the Arctic Ocean. Asia is subdivided into 48 countries, three of them (Russia, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>) having part of their land in Europe.</p>
<p>Asia has extremely diverse climates and geographic features. Climates range from arctic and subarctic in Siberia to tropical in southern India and Southeast Asia. It is moist across southeast sections, and dry across much of the interior. Some of the largest daily temperature ranges on Earth occur in western sections of Asia. The monsoon circulation dominates across southern and eastern sections, due to the presence of the Himalayas forcing the formation of a thermal low which draws in moisture during the summer. Southwestern sections of the continent are hot. Siberia is one of the coldest places in the Northern Hemisphere, and can act as a source of arctic air masses for North America. The most active place on Earth for tropical cyclone activity lies northeast of the Philippines and south of Japan. The <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi Desert</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Desert" title="Arabian Desert">Arabian Desert</a> stretches across much of the Middle East. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a> in China is the longest river in the continent. The <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> between Nepal and China is the tallest mountain range in the world. Tropical rainforests stretch across much of southern Asia and coniferous and deciduous forests lie farther north.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span></h3>
<p>A survey carried out in 2010 by global risk analysis farm <a href="/wiki/Maplecroft" title="Maplecroft">Maplecroft</a> identified 16 countries that are extremely vulnerable to climate change. Each nation's vulnerability was calculated using 42 socio, economic and environmental indicators, which identified the likely climate change impacts during the next 30 years. The Asian countries of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, India, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, Thailand, Pakistan and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> were among the 16 countries facing extreme risk from climate change. Some shifts are already occurring. For example, in tropical parts of India with a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a>, the temperature increased by 0.4 °C between 1901 and 2003. A 2013 study by the <a href="/wiki/International_Crops_Research_Institute_for_the_Semi-Arid_Tropics" title="International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics">International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICRISAT" title="ICRISAT">ICRISAT</a>) aimed to find science-based, pro-poor approaches and techniques that would enable Asia's agricultural systems to cope with climate change, while benefitting poor and vulnerable farmers. The study's recommendations ranged from improving the use of climate information in local planning and strengthening weather-based agro-advisory services, to stimulating diversification of rural household incomes and providing incentives to farmers to adopt natural resource conservation measures to enhance forest cover, replenish groundwater and use <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Asia" title="Economy of Asia">Economy of Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_singapore_city_skyline_dusk_panorama_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2830" data-file-width="4254" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/1_singapore_city_skyline_dusk_panorama_2011.jpg/250px-1_singapore_city_skyline_dusk_panorama_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/1_singapore_city_skyline_dusk_panorama_2011.jpg/375px-1_singapore_city_skyline_dusk_panorama_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/1_singapore_city_skyline_dusk_panorama_2011.jpg/500px-1_singapore_city_skyline_dusk_panorama_2011.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_singapore_city_skyline_dusk_panorama_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Singapore has one of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_port" title="World's busiest port">busiest ports in the world</a> and is the world's fourth largest <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a> trading center.</div>
</div>
</div>

<p>Asia has the second largest <a href="/wiki/Real_versus_nominal_value_(economics)" title="Real versus nominal value (economics)">nominal</a> GDP of all continents, after Europe, but the largest when measured in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. As of 2011, the largest economies in Asia are China, Japan, India, South Korea and Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Based on Global Office Locations 2011, Asia dominated the office locations with 4 of the top 5 being in Asia: Hong Kong, Singapore, Tokyo, <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a> and Shanghai. Around 68 percent of international firms have office in Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the late 1990s and early 2000s, the economies of China<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and India have been growing rapidly, both with an average annual growth rate of more than 8%. Other recent very-high-growth nations in Asia include <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, Pakistan, Thailand, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and the Philippines, and mineral-rich nations such as <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>, Iran, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, Saudi Arabia, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>.</p>
<p>According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_historian" title="Economic historian">economic historian</a> <a href="/wiki/Angus_Maddison" title="Angus Maddison">Angus Maddison</a> in his book <i>The World Economy: A Millennial Perspective</i>, India had the world's largest economy during 0 BCE and 1000 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> China was the <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_China" title="Economic history of China">largest and most advanced economy</a> on earth for much of recorded history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> until the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> (excluding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">India</a>) overtook it in the mid-19th century. For several decades in the late twentieth century Japan was the largest economy in Asia and second-largest of any single nation in the world, after surpassing the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (measured in net material product) in 1986 and Germany in 1968. (NB: A number of supernational economies are larger, such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU), the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA) or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/APEC" title="APEC">APEC</a>). This ended in 2010 when China overtook Japan to become the world's second largest economy.</p>
<p>In the late 1980s and early 1990s, Japan's GDP was almost as large (current exchange rate method) as that of the rest of Asia combined.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1995, Japan's economy nearly equaled that of the USA as the largest economy in the world for a day, after the Japanese currency reached a record high of 79 <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen" title="Japanese yen">yen</a>/US$. Economic growth in Asia since World War II to the 1990s had been concentrated in Japan as well as the four regions of South Korea, Taiwan, Hong Kong and Singapore located in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">Pacific Rim</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Four_Asian_Tigers" title="Four Asian Tigers">Asian tigers</a>, which have now all received developed country status, having the highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_10_skyline_of_Lotus_Colony.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3044" data-file-width="5411" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Mumbai_03-2016_10_skyline_of_Lotus_Colony.jpg/290px-Mumbai_03-2016_10_skyline_of_Lotus_Colony.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Mumbai_03-2016_10_skyline_of_Lotus_Colony.jpg/435px-Mumbai_03-2016_10_skyline_of_Lotus_Colony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Mumbai_03-2016_10_skyline_of_Lotus_Colony.jpg/580px-Mumbai_03-2016_10_skyline_of_Lotus_Colony.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_10_skyline_of_Lotus_Colony.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mumbai is one of the most populous cities on the continent. The city is an infrastructure and tourism hub, and plays a crucial role in the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_India" title="Economy of India">Economy of India</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>It is forecasted that India will overtake Japan in terms of nominal GDP by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> By 2027, according to <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>, China will have the largest economy in the world. Several trade blocs exist, with the most developed being the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a>.</p>
<p>Asia is the largest continent in the world by a considerable margin, and it is rich in natural resources, such as petroleum, forests, fish, water, rice, copper and silver. Manufacturing in Asia has traditionally been strongest in East and Southeast Asia, particularly in China, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, South Korea, Japan, India, the Philippines, and Singapore. Japan and South Korea continue to dominate in the area of <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporations</a>, but increasingly the PRC and India are making significant inroads. Many companies from Europe, North America, South Korea and Japan have operations in Asia's developing countries to take advantage of its abundant supply of cheap labour and relatively developed infrastructure.</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> 9 of 11 <a href="/wiki/3G_(countries)" title="3G (countries)">Global Growth Generators</a> countries came from Asia driven by population and income growth. They are <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, China, India, Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, Mongolia, Philippines, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> and Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Asia has four main financial centers: Tokyo, Hong Kong, Singapore and Shanghai. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Call_center" title="Call center">Call centers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing" title="Business process outsourcing">business process outsourcing</a> (BPOs) are becoming major employers in India and the Philippines due to the availability of a large pool of highly skilled, English-speaking workers. The increased use of outsourcing has assisted the rise of India and the China as financial centers. Due to its large and extremely competitive information technology industry, India has become a major hub for outsourcing.</p>
<p>In 2010, Asia had 3.3 million millionaires (people with net worth over US$1 million excluding their homes), slightly below North America with 3.4 million millionaires. Last year Asia had toppled Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Citigroup in The Wealth Report 2012 stated that Asian centa-millionaire overtook North America's wealth for the first time as the world's "economic center of gravity" continued moving east. At the end of 2011, there were 18,000 Asian people mainly in Southeast Asia, China and Japan who have at least $100 million in disposable assets, while North America with 17,000 people and Western Europe with 14,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Palace_Bangkok.jpg"><img alt="A Thai temple complex with several ornate buildings and a stupa, and a lot of visitors" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1142" data-file-width="1711" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Grand_Palace_Bangkok.jpg/220px-Grand_Palace_Bangkok.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Grand_Palace_Bangkok.jpg/330px-Grand_Palace_Bangkok.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Grand_Palace_Bangkok.jpg/440px-Grand_Palace_Bangkok.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Palace_Bangkok.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wat_Phra_Kaeo" title="Wat Phra Kaeo">Wat Phra Kaeo</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Palace" title="Grand Palace">Grand Palace</a> is among Bangkok's major tourist attractions.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With growing Regional Tourism with domination of Chinese visitors, <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a> has released Global Destination Cities Index 2013 with 10 of 20 are dominated by Asia and Pacific Region Cities and also for the first time a city of a country from Asia (Bangkok) set in the top-ranked with 15.98 international visitors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WorldPopulation.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="916" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/WorldPopulation.png/300px-WorldPopulation.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/WorldPopulation.png/450px-WorldPopulation.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/WorldPopulation.png/600px-WorldPopulation.png 2x" width="300"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WorldPopulation.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Graph showing population by continent as a percentage of <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">world population</a> (1750 - 2005)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>East Asia had by far the strongest overall <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) improvement of any region in the world, nearly doubling average HDI attainment over the past 40 years, according to the report's analysis of health, education and income data. China, the second highest achiever in the world in terms of HDI improvement since 1970, is the only country on the "Top 10 Movers" list due to income rather than health or education achievements. Its per capita income increased a stunning 21-fold over the last four decades, also lifting hundreds of millions out of income poverty. Yet it was not among the region's top performers in improving school enrollment and life expectancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-53">[53]</a></sup><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, a South Asian country, emerges as one of the world's fastest movers since 1970 mainly due to health and education achievements. Its present <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> is 25 years longer than in the 1970s. More than four of every five children of school age in Nepal now attend primary school, compared to just one in five 40 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-53">[53]</a></sup><br/>
Japan and South Korea ranked highest among the countries grouped on the HDI (number 11 and 12 in the world, which are in the "very high human development" category), followed by Hong Kong (21) and Singapore (27). <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> (155) ranked lowest amongst Asian countries out of the 169 countries assessed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Asia" title="Languages of Asia">Languages of Asia</a></div>
<p>Asia is home to several <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">language families</a> and many <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">language isolates</a>. Most Asian countries have more than one language that is natively spoken. For instance, according to <a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">Ethnologue</a>, more than 600 languages are spoken in Indonesia, more than 800 languages spoken in India, and more than 100 are spoken in the Philippines. China has many languages and dialects in different provinces.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_philosophy" title="Eastern philosophy">Eastern philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Asia" title="Religion in Asia">Religion in Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Asian_mythologies" title="List of Asian mythologies">List of Asian mythologies</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spring_Temple_Buddha_picturing_Vairocana,_in_Lushan_County,_Henan,_China.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="426" height="337" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Spring_Temple_Buddha_picturing_Vairocana%2C_in_Lushan_County%2C_Henan%2C_China.png/220px-Spring_Temple_Buddha_picturing_Vairocana%2C_in_Lushan_County%2C_Henan%2C_China.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Spring_Temple_Buddha_picturing_Vairocana%2C_in_Lushan_County%2C_Henan%2C_China.png/330px-Spring_Temple_Buddha_picturing_Vairocana%2C_in_Lushan_County%2C_Henan%2C_China.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Spring_Temple_Buddha_picturing_Vairocana%2C_in_Lushan_County%2C_Henan%2C_China.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spring_Temple_Buddha_picturing_Vairocana,_in_Lushan_County,_Henan,_China.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Spring_Temple_Buddha" title="Spring Temple Buddha">Spring Temple Buddha</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lushan_County,_Henan" title="Lushan County, Henan">Lushan County, Henan</a>, China is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_statues_by_height" title="List of statues by height">world's tallest statue</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many of the world's <a href="/wiki/Major_religious_groups" title="Major religious groups">major religions</a> have their origins in Asia, including the five most practiced in the world (excluding <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">irreligion</a>), which are Christianity, Islam, Hinduism, Chinese folk religion (classified as Confucianism and Taoism), and Buddhism respectively. Asian mythology is complex and diverse. The story of the <a href="/wiki/Flood_myth" title="Flood myth">Great Flood</a> for example, as presented to Christians in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a> in the narrative of <a href="/wiki/Noah" title="Noah">Noah</a>, is first found in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesopotamian_mythology" title="Mesopotamian mythology">Mesopotamian mythology</a>, in the <i><a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh" title="Epic of Gilgamesh">Epic of Gilgamesh</a></i>. Likewise, the same story of <a href="/wiki/Flood_myth" title="Flood myth">Great Flood</a> is presented to Muslims in the Holy <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a>, again in the narrative of <a href="/wiki/Noah" title="Noah">Noah</a>, Who according to <a href="/wiki/Islamic_mythology" title="Islamic mythology">Islamic mythology</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Prophet" title="Prophet">Prophet</a> and Built an Ark on <a href="/wiki/Allah" title="Allah">Allah</a>'s Command to save the True Believers from the Great Flood (Great Calamity).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hindu_mythology" title="Hindu mythology">Hindu mythology</a> also tells about an <a href="/wiki/Avatar" title="Avatar">Avatar</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">God Vishnu</a> in the form of a <a href="/wiki/Matsya" title="Matsya">fish</a> who warned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sraddhadeva_Manu" title="Sraddhadeva Manu">Manu</a> of a terrible flood. In ancient <a href="/wiki/Chinese_mythology" title="Chinese mythology">Chinese mythology</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shan_Hai_Jing" title="Shan Hai Jing">Shan Hai Jing</a>, the Chinese ruler <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Yu_of_Xia_of_China" title="King Yu of Xia of China">Da Yu</a>, had to spend 10 years to control a deluge which swept out most of ancient China and was aided by the goddess <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCwa" title="Nüwa">Nüwa</a> who literally fixed the broken sky through which huge rains were pouring.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Abrahamic">Abrahamic</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religions" title="Abrahamic religions">Abrahamic religions</a> including Judaism, Christianity, Islam and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'í Faith</a> originated in West Asia.</p>
<p>Judaism, the oldest of the Abrahamic faiths, is practiced primarily in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, the birthplace and historical homeland of the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Hebrew nation</a> which today consists equally of those <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a> who remained in <a href="/wiki/Mizrahi_Jews" title="Mizrahi Jews">Asia/North Africa</a> and those who returned from <a href="/wiki/Jewish_diaspora" title="Jewish diaspora">diaspora</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">North America</a>, and other regions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> though sizable communities continue to live abroad. Jews are the predominant ethnic group in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> (75.6%) numbering at about 6.1 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> although the levels of adherence to Jewish religion are unspecified. Outside of Israel there are small ancient communities of Jewish still live in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (17,400),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary-57">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> (9,100),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mashke2_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-mashke2-58">[58]</a></sup> Iran (8,756),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IranCensusMurder_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-IranCensusMurder-59">[59]</a></sup> India (5,000) and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> (4,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Christianity is a widespread religion in Asia with more than 286 million adherents according to <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> and nearly 364 million according to <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Britannica</a> Book of the Year 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Constituting around 12.6% of the total population of Asia. In the Philippines and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>, Roman Catholicism is the predominant religion; it was introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spaniards</a> and the Portuguese, respectively. In <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, Georgia and Asian Russia, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a> is the predominant religion. Various Christian <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">denominations</a> have adherents in portions of the Middle East, as well as China and India. <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas_Christians" title="Saint Thomas Christians">Saint Thomas Christians</a> in India trace their origins to the evangelistic activity of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_the_Apostle" title="Thomas the Apostle">Thomas the Apostle</a> in the 1st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Islam, which originated in Saudi Arabia, is the largest and most widely spread religion in Asia with at least 1 billion Muslims constituting around 23.8% of the total population of Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> With 12.7% of the world Muslim population, the country currently with the largest Muslim population in the world is Indonesia, followed by Pakistan, India, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, Iran and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">Medina</a> and to a lesser extent Jerusalem are the holiest cities for Islam in all the world. These religious sites attract large numbers of devotees from all over the world, particularly during the <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Umrah</a> seasons. Iran is the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shi%27a" title="Shi'a">Shi'a</a> country.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'í Faith</a> originated in Asia, in Iran (Persia), and spread from there to the Ottoman Empire, Central Asia, India, and Burma during the lifetime of Bahá'u'lláh. Since the middle of the 20th century, growth has particularly occurred in other Asian countries, because Bahá'í activities in many Muslim countries has been severely <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%ADs" title="Persecution of Bahá'ís">suppressed</a> by authorities. <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Temple" title="Lotus Temple">Lotus Temple</a> is a big Baha'i Temple in India.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_and_East_Asian_religions">Indian and East Asian religions</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akshardham_Lotus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="327" data-file-width="435" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Akshardham_Lotus.jpg/220px-Akshardham_Lotus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Akshardham_Lotus.jpg/330px-Akshardham_Lotus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/Akshardham_Lotus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akshardham_Lotus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swaminarayan_Hinduism" title="Swaminarayan Hinduism">Swaminarayan</a> <a href="/wiki/Akshardham_(Delhi)" title="Akshardham (Delhi)">Akshardham Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Record" title="Guinness World Record">Guinness World Records</a> is the <i>World's Largest Comprehensive Hindu Temple</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Almost all Asian religions have philosophical character and Asian philosophical traditions cover a large spectrum of philosophical thoughts and writings. <a href="/wiki/Indian_philosophy" title="Indian philosophy">Indian philosophy</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Hindu_philosophy" title="Hindu philosophy">Hindu philosophy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_philosophy" title="Buddhist philosophy">Buddhist philosophy</a>. They include elements of nonmaterial pursuits, whereas another school of thought from India, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C4%81rv%C4%81ka" title="Cārvāka">Cārvāka</a>, preached the enjoyment of the material world. The religions of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> originated in India, South Asia. In East Asia, particularly in China and Japan, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zen" title="Zen">Zen Buddhism</a> took shape.</p>
<p>As of 2012, Hinduism has around 1.1 billion adherents. The faith represents around 25% of Asia's population and is the second largest religion in Asia. However, it is mostly concentrated in South Asia. Over 80% of the populations of both India and Nepal adhere to Hinduism, alongside significant communities in Bangladesh, Pakistan, Bhutan, Sri Lanka and <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>, Indonesia. Many overseas Indians in countries such as Burma, Singapore and Malaysia also adhere to Hinduism.</p>
<p>Buddhism has a great following in mainland Southeast Asia and East Asia. Buddhism is the religion of the majority of the populations of <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> (96%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> (95%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a> (80%–89%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Japan (36%–96%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> (75%–84%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> (70%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> (60%–67%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> (53%–93%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Large Buddhist populations also exist in Singapore (33%–51%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> (35%–93%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> South Korea (23%–50%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> (19%–21%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> (9%–11%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> (10%–75%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> China (20%–50%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> (1.5%–14%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and small communities in India and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>. In many Chinese communities, Mahayana Buddhism is easily syncretized with Taoism, thus exact religious statistics is difficult to obtain and may be understated or overstated. The Communist-governed countries of China, Vietnam and North Korea are officially atheist, thus the number of Buddhists and other religious adherents may be under-reported.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> is found mainly in India and in oversea Indian communities such as the United States and Malaysia. <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> is found in Northern India and amongst overseas Indian communities in other parts of Asia, especially Southeast Asia. <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> is found predominantly in Mainland China, South Korea, Taiwan and in overseas Chinese populations. Taoism is found mainly in Mainland China, Taiwan, Malaysia and Singapore. Taoism is easily syncretized with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism" title="Mahayana Buddhism">Mahayana Buddhism</a> for many Chinese, thus exact religious statistics is difficult to obtain and may be understated or overstated.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_conflicts">Modern conflicts</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Napalm.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="587" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Napalm.jpg/220px-Napalm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Napalm.jpg/330px-Napalm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Napalm.jpg/440px-Napalm.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Napalm.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
US forces drop <a href="/wiki/Napalm" title="Napalm">Napalm</a> on suspected <a href="/wiki/Viet_Cong" title="Viet Cong">Viet Cong</a> positions in 1965</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wounded_civilians_arrive_at_hospital_Aleppo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="718" data-file-width="1277" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Wounded_civilians_arrive_at_hospital_Aleppo.jpg/220px-Wounded_civilians_arrive_at_hospital_Aleppo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Wounded_civilians_arrive_at_hospital_Aleppo.jpg/330px-Wounded_civilians_arrive_at_hospital_Aleppo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Wounded_civilians_arrive_at_hospital_Aleppo.jpg/440px-Wounded_civilians_arrive_at_hospital_Aleppo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
