<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_prizes">Nobel prizes</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="280" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg/170px-Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg/255px-Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/91/Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rabindranath_Tagore_in_1909.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bengali polymath <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a> was awarded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Literature" title="Nobel Prize for Literature">Nobel Prize for Literature</a> in 1913, and became Asia's first Nobel laureate</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymath</a> <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bengali_literature" title="Bengali literature">Bengali</a> poet, dramatist, and writer from <a href="/wiki/Santiniketan" title="Santiniketan">Santiniketan</a>, now in <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>, India, became in 1913 the first Asian <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureate</a>. He won his <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> for notable impact his prose works and poetic thought had on English, French, and other national literatures of Europe and the Americas. He is also the writer of the national anthems of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and India.</p>
<p>Other Asian writers who won Nobel Prize for literature include <a href="/wiki/Yasunari_Kawabata" title="Yasunari Kawabata">Yasunari Kawabata</a> (Japan, 1968), <a href="/wiki/Kenzabur%C5%8D_%C5%8Ce" title="Kenzaburō Ōe">Kenzaburō Ōe</a> (Japan, 1994), <a href="/wiki/Gao_Xingjian" title="Gao Xingjian">Gao Xingjian</a> (China, 2000), <a href="/wiki/Orhan_Pamuk" title="Orhan Pamuk">Orhan Pamuk</a> (Turkey, 2006), and <a href="/wiki/Mo_Yan" title="Mo Yan">Mo Yan</a> (China, 2012). Some may consider the American writer, <a href="/wiki/Pearl_S._Buck" title="Pearl S. Buck">Pearl S. Buck</a>, an honorary Asian Nobel laureate, having spent considerable time in China as the daughter of missionaries, and based many of her novels, namely <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Earth" title="The Good Earth">The Good Earth</a></i> (1931) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Mother_(1934_novel)" title="The Mother (1934 novel)">The Mother</a></i> (1933), as well as the biographies of her parents of their time in China, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Exile_(1936_book)" title="The Exile (1936 book)">The Exile</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Fighting_Angel" title="Fighting Angel">Fighting Angel</a></i>, all of which earned her the Literature prize in 1938.</p>
<p>Also, <a href="/wiki/Mother_Teresa" title="Mother Teresa">Mother Teresa</a> of India and <a href="/wiki/Shirin_Ebadi" title="Shirin Ebadi">Shirin Ebadi</a> of Iran were awarded the Nobel Peace Prize for their significant and pioneering efforts for democracy and human rights, especially for the rights of women and children. Ebadi is the first Iranian and the first Muslim woman to receive the prize. Another Nobel Peace Prize winner is <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a> for her peaceful and non-violent struggle under a military dictatorship in Burma. She is a nonviolent pro-democracy activist and leader of the National League for Democracy in Burma (Myanmar) and a noted prisoner of conscience. She is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> and was awarded the Nobel Peace Prize in 1991. Chinese dissident <a href="/wiki/Liu_Xiaobo" title="Liu Xiaobo">Liu Xiaobo</a> was awarded the Nobel Peace Prize for "his long and non-violent struggle for fundamental human rights in China" on 8 October 2010. He is the first Chinese citizen to be awarded a Nobel Prize of any kind while residing in China. In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Kailash_Satyarthi" title="Kailash Satyarthi">Kailash Satyarthi</a> from India and <a href="/wiki/Malala_Yousafzai" title="Malala Yousafzai">Malala Yousafzai</a> from Pakistan were awarded the Nobel Peace Prize "for their struggle against the suppression of children and young people and for the right of all children to education".</p>
<p>Sir <a href="/wiki/C._V._Raman" title="C. V. Raman">C. V. Raman</a> is the first Asian to get a Nobel prize in Sciences. He won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> "for his work on the scattering of light and for the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Raman_scattering" title="Raman scattering">effect named after him</a>".</p>
<p>Japan has won the most Nobel Prizes of any Asian nation with 24 followed by India which has won 13.</p>
<p>Amartya Sen, (born 3 November 1933) is an Indian economist who was awarded the 1998 Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences for his contributions to welfare economics and <a href="/wiki/Social_choice_theory" title="Social choice theory">social choice theory</a>, and for his interest in the problems of society's poorest members.</p>
<p>Other Asian Nobel Prize winners include <a href="/wiki/Subrahmanyan_Chandrasekhar" title="Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar">Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdus_Salam" title="Abdus Salam">Abdus Salam</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malala_yousafzai" title="Malala yousafzai">Malala yousafzai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Aumann" title="Robert Aumann">Robert Aumann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">Menachem Begin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Ciechanover" title="Aaron Ciechanover">Aaron Ciechanover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avram_Hershko" title="Avram Hershko">Avram Hershko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Kahneman" title="Daniel Kahneman">Daniel Kahneman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">Shimon Peres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">Yitzhak Rabin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ada_Yonath" title="Ada Yonath">Ada Yonath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ramos-Horta" title="José Ramos-Horta">José Ramos-Horta</a> and Bishop <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Filipe_Ximenes_Belo" title="Carlos Filipe Ximenes Belo">Carlos Filipe Ximenes Belo</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timor_Leste" title="Timor Leste">Timor Leste</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Dae-jung" title="Kim Dae-jung">Kim Dae-jung</a>, and 13 Japanese scientists. Most of the said awardees are from Japan and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> except for Chandrasekhar and Raman (India), Abdus Salam and Malala yousafzai, (Pakistan), Arafat (Palestinian Territories), Kim (South Korea), and Horta and Belo (Timor Leste).</p>
<p>In 2006, Dr. <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> was awarded the Nobel Peace Prize for the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Grameen_Bank" title="Grameen Bank">Grameen Bank</a>, a community development bank that lends money to poor people, especially women in Bangladesh. Dr. Yunus received his PhD in economics from Vanderbilt University, United States. He is internationally known for the concept of micro credit which allows poor and destitute people with little or no collateral to borrow money. The borrowers typically pay back money within the specified period and the incidence of default is very low.</p>
<p>The Dalai Lama has received approximately eighty-four awards over his spiritual and political career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On 22 June 2006, he became one of only four people ever to be recognized with Honorary Citizenship by the Governor General of Canada. On 28 May 2005, he received the Christmas Humphreys Award from the Buddhist Society in the United Kingdom. Most notable was the Nobel Peace Prize, presented in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oslo,_Norway" title="Oslo, Norway">Oslo, Norway</a> on 10 December 1989.</p>
